  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_33a6ce1c-c4dc-43d7-a787-352ad8690c0a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1278337990088647035">The Blue Bloods have powers beyond human comprehension: strength that defies logic, speed that cannot be captured on film, the ability to shape-shift, and more. But in matters of the heart, no one, not even those immortal vampires, has total control.<br/><br/>In <i>Bloody Valentine</i>, part of the best-selling Blue Bloods series, author Melissa de la Cruz offers three tantalizing stories </span>
  <span id="freeText1278337990088647035" style="display:none">The Blue Bloods have powers beyond human comprehension: strength that defies logic, speed that cannot be captured on film, the ability to shape-shift, and more. But in matters of the heart, no one, not even those immortal vampires, has total control.<br /><br />In <i>Bloody Valentine</i>, part of the best-selling Blue Bloods series, author Melissa de la Cruz offers three tantalizing stories that delve deep into the love lives of the all-powerful vamps (and their Red Blood friends) from New York's Upper East Side. Might a witchy new girl help cure Oliver's broken heart? How did Allegra fall in love with a human? Will Schuyler and Jack finally be bonded?<br /><br />Romantic and sensual, <i>Bloody Valentine</i> reveals the undying love, the hope and devastation, and the lust and longing that have defined the Blue Bloods throughout history. Prepare to be swept off your feet.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2384703868?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2384703868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8071911147126089106">Bloody Valentine is a little book full of short stories relating to romance in the Blue Bloods universe.<br/><br/>I meant to read this years ago, but it disappeared into the depths of my book shelf. I finally found it the other day, and I decided I might as well read it. I'm sure, somewhere, I have the remaining books of the Blue Bloods I meant to years...half a decade ago...<br/><br/>The short stories were cute, but I don't remember half of what happened in the Blue Bloods universe. With that being said, I wouldn'</span>
  <span id="freeText8071911147126089106" style="display:none">Bloody Valentine is a little book full of short stories relating to romance in the Blue Bloods universe.<br /><br />I meant to read this years ago, but it disappeared into the depths of my book shelf. I finally found it the other day, and I decided I might as well read it. I'm sure, somewhere, I have the remaining books of the Blue Bloods I meant to years...half a decade ago...<br /><br />The short stories were cute, but I don't remember half of what happened in the Blue Bloods universe. With that being said, I wouldn't recommend reading this book outside of the series. Make sure you are reading the series so you understand everything that is happening. I did a little research on Goodreads to review what had been happening in the series so far, but it would make way more sense to read it within the series.<br /><br />Oliver, Allegra and Schuyler's stories were adorable and sweet, and I think this is a great addition to the series. I'd like more sweet stories like this for other series as well!! <br /><br />Overall, it was cute and I enjoyed it. It's definitely just some YA side stories so it's not a must read for me by any means. If you're into the Blue Bloods, this is for you. It's vampires, ooey gooey romance, excessive drama, and lots of gossip! What else can you ask for from a YA board school-esque story? It's like Gossip Girl and Vampire Diaries had a baby.<br /><br />Three out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8071911147126089106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2064349301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5584412847762839122">Bloody Valentine delivers where Keys to the Repository was lacking. Actual novellas about some of my faves!! Novellas to fill in the blanks and give me more of what I was missing from the stories!!! AND YET I WAS SO UNSATISFIED. <br/><br/>I’ll break it down by novellas for ya because each one was TRULY a disaster in it’s own way.<br/>1.	The Oliver centered novella explains how he will be able to move on from Schyler. To put it simply I think this could have been handled in a much better way. It was so OOC, ent</span>
  <span id="freeText5584412847762839122" style="display:none">Bloody Valentine delivers where Keys to the Repository was lacking. Actual novellas about some of my faves!! Novellas to fill in the blanks and give me more of what I was missing from the stories!!! AND YET I WAS SO UNSATISFIED. <br /><br />I’ll break it down by novellas for ya because each one was TRULY a disaster in it’s own way.<br />1.	The Oliver centered novella explains how he will be able to move on from Schyler. To put it simply I think this could have been handled in a much better way. It was so OOC, entirely to convenient and also I’m pretty sure it was just here so that MDLC could give a shout out to her spin off series. All things considered I was actually intrigued by the character introduced in this one and so yeah it worked I’ll probably read the spin off series. But this story wasn’t necessary, I didn’t want or need it, definitely could have lived with out it. <br />2.	This one was actually pretty cute. Explained a lot about Allegra, but the ending made absolutely no sense in terms of the actual series. It didn’t line up with how the rest of the series goes and unless I misread it I don’t understand why the author had this happen the way it did. Left me with more questions than answers. <i> Okay that’s not true, it answered some questions buuuuut left me with new ones </i><br />3.	THIS ONE HAD SO MUCH POTENTIAL. It was supposed to be so cute and great and this was literally the only one I was looking forward too and we had to go and add unnecessary plot? I literally just wanted cute fluff and instead I got unnecessary drama that literally added NOTHING to the series !!!!! At least the first two added something even if they were annoying?? The drama in this DID NOT A SINGLE THING OTHER THAN MAKE THIS LONGER THAN IT NEEDED TO BE. The ending was cute tho, I’m just mad that the novella was pointless when it could have literally just be cute fluff. <br /><br />Basically I just wish all these novellas were delivered differently. 2 stars because in general I liked the end result I just wish they were handled better. <br /></span>

    <a title="Heidi McLaughlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3333952-heidi-mclaughlin"><img alt="Heidi McLaughlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461629210p2/3333952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136730779?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi McLaughlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi McLaughlin" href="/user/show/3333952-heidi-mclaughlin">Heidi McLaughlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer136730779&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136730779" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14270387012791202891">I have been on pins and needles waiting for Bloody Valentine, the current installment of Melissa de la Cruz hit series Blue Bloods. And it's finally out today!<br/><br/>It took me just over an hour to read the book because it's that good. From the first page (with Oliver battling his inner demon) to the last (which I won't spoil), I just couldn't put it down.<br/><br/>In Bloody Valentine, the author introduces us to a new character: Freya. Right away, I knew I'd like her (which just increases my anticipation for th</span>
  <span id="freeText14270387012791202891" style="display:none">I have been on pins and needles waiting for Bloody Valentine, the current installment of Melissa de la Cruz hit series Blue Bloods. And it's finally out today!<br /><br />It took me just over an hour to read the book because it's that good. From the first page (with Oliver battling his inner demon) to the last (which I won't spoil), I just couldn't put it down.<br /><br />In Bloody Valentine, the author introduces us to a new character: Freya. Right away, I knew I'd like her (which just increases my anticipation for the release of The Witches of East End which comes out in the June 21, 2011)...<br /><br />Back for some added dimension are Allegra and Charles mixed with a little Bendix Chase, who happens to be Schuyler's father.<br /><br />We'll also go to Endicott College, where Allegra falls in love and performs a Sacred Kiss that allows her to see what her life will be like. Of course, this portion of the novel isn't complete without Cordelia. We're given a very compelling glimpse into the twins' cycle mother... and she's pretty feisty.<br /><br />Finally, Jack and Schuyler! Two of my favorite couples in the literary world are finally headed for a major commitment, but I'll let you read the book to see how it all plays out. I promise it won't disappoint!<br /><br />Also, be sure to check out <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thevanalenlegacy.com">www.thevanalenlegacy.com:</a> a site dedicated to the series</span>

<div id="review_95888245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95888245" />
    <a title="Marija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3450964-marija"><img alt="Marija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314915186p2/3450964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95888245?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marija" href="/user/show/3450964-marija">Marija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3450964-marija?shelf=ya-mg">ya-mg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3450964-marija?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95888245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12883472157612718123">Why do I like this book and for that matter this series? I can’t explain it. It’s against all sense and reason. It’s sort of like my feelings for Shakespeare’s character Falstaff. He’s a real rogue, an old dirty letch… fat and sweaty always up to some kind of scheme to make a fast buck. Yet I can’t help loving the bastard. It’s crazy. <br/><br/>This book is the same… lousy title, over the top and unnecessary melodrama, some cringeworthy scenes, and cheesy illustrations. Yet after finishing the three stori</span>
  <span id="freeText12883472157612718123" style="display:none">Why do I like this book and for that matter this series? I can’t explain it. It’s against all sense and reason. It’s sort of like my feelings for Shakespeare’s character Falstaff. He’s a real rogue, an old dirty letch… fat and sweaty always up to some kind of scheme to make a fast buck. Yet I can’t help loving the bastard. It’s crazy. <br /><br />This book is the same… lousy title, over the top and unnecessary melodrama, some cringeworthy scenes, and cheesy illustrations. Yet after finishing the three stories that make up this tiny book, I had a traitorous half-grin on my face. What a bitch.<br /><br />If de la Cruz edited out some of that superfluous drama, these stories could have easily been included in the series proper or at least have been present in her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7031834.Keys_to_the_Repository__A_Blue_Blood_Companion_Book_" title="Keys to the Repository (A Blue Blood Companion Book) by Melissa de la Cruz" rel="nofollow noopener">Keys to the Repository</a> file guide. The first story details how Oliver was able to move on from the “loss” of Schuyler. It’s also a vehicle to promote her new adult series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9464745.Witches_of_East_End" title="Witches of East End by Melissa de la Cruz" rel="nofollow noopener">Witches of East End</a>. It certainly has more of that adult novel feel to it, but I don’t know… in this case I think a more subtle approach to the writing would have said more and have felt less trashy. The initial descriptions of Oliver’s spiral into depression were quite good, since there’s some depth in regards to the writing. But after that, the writing loses momentum, focusing on unnecessary details that left strange images in my mind's eye. As is, it does offer some explanations, but I think the story could have been handled much better. <br /><br />The second story details how Schuyler’s parents met. This story is actually the weakest of the three, leaving you with more questions that haven’t yet been answered. Also, de la Cruz’s portrayal of Allegra is crappy. She’s just a blonde Barbie doll, with no real substance, only considering her own needs. She reminds me of Bliss, but I think Allegra’s worse. I find this strange, since Allegra’s voice here doesn’t really match the voice of Tomasia—Allegra’s former self in a previous lifecycle (described in book five). Tomasia seemed to have more substance. I guess after the events in Florence, which supposedly lead to Bliss’s birth, Allegra’s character and soul regressed to a shallow mindless girl. ;) And Charles, her twin, is a true emotional mess. What a whiny puppy! Though I did foresee something like this when de la Cruz changed her story in <i>Keys</i>, i.e. making Charles Allegra’s twin, instead of the older brother that was initially described in the early books of the series. The descriptions of Ben, Sky’s father, are rather strange, though it does seem to support my theory about his true identity—which I formed after reading book five. If you’re looking for answers from this story, don’t expect them here. <br /><br />The third story is the promised Jack and Schuyler bonding ceremony. Truly, if de la Cruz edited out all of the action sequences, which essentially makes the story feel like a cheap action flick, it could’ve easily been included in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7747263.Misguided_Angel__Blue_Bloods___5_" title="Misguided Angel (Blue Bloods, #5) by Melissa de la Cruz" rel="nofollow noopener">Misguided Angel</a>. I understand why she includes these sequences—due to the final reveal at the end—but for me it just kills the story. The illustrations—which only appear here—are fine, but when I first noticed them in my initial flip through, I just cringed... more unnecessary details. Do I really understand how this bonding was possible given the vampire mythology de la Cruz provides? Not really, it’s still a muddle in my mind. Yet, hell, I found myself loving that sappy conclusion. Reason says stop right here, no more, but somehow I just can’t. I guess this means I’ll be tuning in to the next book in the series whenever it arrives.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12883472157612718123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_220524035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220524035" />
    <a title="Parvathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy"><img alt="Parvathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425840439p2/4915009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220524035?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parvathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parvathy" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy">Parvathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Blue Bloods series fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Parvathy by: </span>
      goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=vampires-everywhere">vampires-everywhere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=broken-characters">broken-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220524035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1600045119879651515">It was necessity that made me read this book. I am not much of a fan of book that are not the next in the series or a spin off but something in between. But this series is so complicated that it is very difficult to keep track of all the things that happened. Since I am planning on reading <b> Lost in Time </b> the next in the Blue Blood series soon and have no detailed recollection of the things that happened in the previous books I decided to give this one try hoping for a little memory jolt. Well th</span>
  <span id="freeText1600045119879651515" style="display:none">It was necessity that made me read this book. I am not much of a fan of book that are not the next in the series or a spin off but something in between. But this series is so complicated that it is very difficult to keep track of all the things that happened. Since I am planning on reading <b> Lost in Time </b> the next in the Blue Blood series soon and have no detailed recollection of the things that happened in the previous books I decided to give this one try hoping for a little memory jolt. Well that was my intention but what happened was it left me in a state more confused than ever. Other than adding more questions to my already long list of questions the book did little more than remind me the names of all the characters. Now you might ask me why I keep on reading this series if it this complicated?? and the simple explanation is the story is good. The concept is different and has this certain quality that makes you want to hang on. Even though Bloody Valentine failed to fulfill the purpose I intended it for it was not entirely a fail. Bloody Valentine is more like a continuation story rather than a recollection as I was hoping for. This contained three short stories which provided further insight in to some of the well loved characters. The first one is about Oliver as he tries to come in terms with his grief regarding the loss of Schuyler and his recovery. Though I was happy for Oliver the latter felt more like a promotional stunt for the author's next series. The next story is about Allegra Van Allen <i> Schuyler's Mom </i> and how she met <i> Schuyler's Dad </i>. Talk about cliffhangers, I am at loss when it comes to understanding the purpose of this story if the author never intended to give it a satisfying end. Then all those times Allegra kept thinking about her life cycle in Florence as though it was a turning point in the whole story I kept thinking what happened in Florence. Then I had this strange recollection of a story line taking place in Florence that was mentioned in <b>Misguided Angel</b><s>I think</s>. Now I am searching for the plot summary of <b>Misguided Angel</b> to make heads or tails of the situation. Maybe I should write down the important points when it comes to this series. Then the third story is about the bonding ceremony between Schuyler and Jack. The author requires some credit here, ending with this particular story because it will help keep the readers interested until the next book is released. But there are a number of things utterly unbelievable about this story and one of those is how any one can that easily fall in and out of love. You have to read the story to know what I am taking about. I was a little disappointed on not encountering Mimi in this book. After the <b> Misguided Angel</b> and getting a taste of the Mimi Force debacle I was hoping for more. Bloody Valentine is not without its merits but it is more of like a glorified prologue for <b>Lost in Time</b> and those who are following this series should not miss this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1600045119879651515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117024413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117024413" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117024413?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423142645" href="/book/show/8372608-bloody-valentine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=angelology">angelology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=romance-novel">romance-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117024413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12459579519749818313"><b>”Bloody Valentine”</b> is a novella in the Blue Bloods series. It consists of three beautifully written short stories each with a focus on matters of the heart--hence the title. While it is not necessary to have read all the books in this series before reading this novella, it is recommended, as two of the three stories relate to events that take place in the previous two books. <br/><br/>The first story is about Schuyler Van Alen's friend and familiar Oliver Hazard-Perry and Freya, a character who will be th</span>
  <span id="freeText12459579519749818313" style="display:none"><b>”Bloody Valentine”</b> is a novella in the Blue Bloods series. It consists of three beautifully written short stories each with a focus on matters of the heart--hence the title. While it is not necessary to have read all the books in this series before reading this novella, it is recommended, as two of the three stories relate to events that take place in the previous two books. <br /><br />The first story is about Schuyler Van Alen's friend and familiar Oliver Hazard-Perry and Freya, a character who will be the focus of a new series by the author entitled <b>”Witches of East End”</b> (which I’ll probably check out to see it it’s worth reading). It is a wonderful story that fills in some of the missing pieces on what's going on with Oliver at the same time as other things are occurring in <b>”Misguided Angel”</b>. <br /><br />The second story brings us back to 1985 where we get to meet a young Allegra Van Alen and the human familiar she falls in love with, Bendix Chase. This is a great addition as it gives further insight into Schuyler's parents and just how she came to be. I really enjoyed this story since thus far in the series we haven’t been given much info about Allegra’s life before being in the hospital. <br /><br />The final story, and the longest, is about Schuyler Van Alen and Jack Force and their bonding ceremony which occurs after the events in <b>”Misguided Angel”</b>. This is a great way to close this book as it gives readers another opportunity to see Jack and Schuyler and witness their love for one another. It bridges the long gap between the previous book and the next book in the series, <b>”Lost in Time”</b>, which won't be out until October.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong the content was as great as always, but the style of the books has changed a lot and they seem to be getting shorter and shorter.<br /><br /><br />More of Purplycookie’s Reviews @: <b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/purplycookie">http://www.goodreads.com/purplycookie</a> </b><br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> Bloody Valentine (A Blue Bloods Book)<br /><u>Author</u> Melissa De La Cruz<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="12459579519749818313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146010232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146010232" />
    <a title="Courtney Hawkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3996043-courtney-hawkins"><img alt="Courtney Hawkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596659860p2/3996043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146010232?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney Hawkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney Hawkins" href="/user/show/3996043-courtney-hawkins">Courtney Hawkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146010232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2978939127542079727">Where to Begin.... I was deeply disappointed by this book. I feel like Melissa De La Cruz might be losing her touch with this series which saddens me because it's my favorite book series to date. This book (which isn't really a book) is just a collection of three short stories. All the short stories felt extremely rush and forced.<br/><br/>The first story follows Oliver and his life after Schuyler leaves. This felt out of character for Oliver, to me. I found myself actually laughing at how ridiculous the </span>
  <span id="freeText2978939127542079727" style="display:none">Where to Begin.... I was deeply disappointed by this book. I feel like Melissa De La Cruz might be losing her touch with this series which saddens me because it's my favorite book series to date. This book (which isn't really a book) is just a collection of three short stories. All the short stories felt extremely rush and forced.<br /><br />The first story follows Oliver and his life after Schuyler leaves. This felt out of character for Oliver, to me. I found myself actually laughing at how ridiculous the story line was until I saw the last page of the story and then it made sense. I suppose it was a very good idea but it would have been better if it were longer. This is the type if storyline that should be in the book itself, not written as a short story.<br /><br />The second story is about how Allegra falls in love with a red blood. This was my favorite story of the three and it felt the most natural. It was nice to see into Allegra's past. We hear lots of odd and ends about it in the series but never actually venture into how and why it happened. This short story does which was actually very refreshing.<br /><br />The third is Jack and Schuyler's bonding. I used to be a very big Jack and Schuyler shipper but they've just gotten... bland. I feel like they are one person now. This story line felt the most rushed of all. It would have been better as a story line in an actual book. It reminded me of watching a movie on fast forward. You see the overall picture but you miss all the detail.<br /><br />There were also a few drawings in the book of Jack and Schuyler and I felt like they were just there to take up space on the page. I would rather wait longer for an actual good book that contributes to the series than Melissa pumping out these mediocre (and pricey) companion books to make the wait seem lesser. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2978939127542079727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153887033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153887033" />
    <a title="Stacey O&#39;Neale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3856654-stacey-o-neale"><img alt="Stacey O&#39;Neale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442962925p2/3856654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153887033?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey O&#39;Neale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey O&#39;Neale" href="/user/show/3856654-stacey-o-neale">Stacey O&#39;Neale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153887033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11079955091991401773">Review written by the YA Fantasy Guide staff reviewer, Camille Morales.<br/><br/>Bloody valentine is a Blue Bloods novella. I am a huge fan of the series, so I was thrilled to finally read this book. I’d been waiting a long time to get it. It was totally worth it.<br/>This book will not be your normal Blue Bloods book, because it is divided in three parts, and each part tells a different story. The parts tell: what happens to Oliver after Schuyler leaves with Jack, how Allegra and Schuyler’s father met, and Sc</span>
  <span id="freeText11079955091991401773" style="display:none">Review written by the YA Fantasy Guide staff reviewer, Camille Morales.<br /><br />Bloody valentine is a Blue Bloods novella. I am a huge fan of the series, so I was thrilled to finally read this book. I’d been waiting a long time to get it. It was totally worth it.<br />This book will not be your normal Blue Bloods book, because it is divided in three parts, and each part tells a different story. The parts tell: what happens to Oliver after Schuyler leaves with Jack, how Allegra and Schuyler’s father met, and Schuyler and Jack’s bonding. It does not follow where Misguided Angel left off. <br /><br />The one I enjoyed most was Allegra’s and Schuyler’s father’s story. It was just so amazing how they got to know each other. They’d already known who they were, and had seen each other, but never really got to know each other. In this story, it tells you how they got to know each other. You get to see more about Charles Van Alen also. It was a really, really good story. <br /><br />My least favorite, though, was Oliver’s. Before I read it, I’d thought my least favorite was going to be the bonding between Jack and Schuyler, because I like having them deal with the whole forbidden love thing. But, now they are bonded. But, the way this book ends, it makes the whole bonding make sense. <br /><br />Okay, so Oliver’s story is basically about how he deals with life without Schuyler, and how he goes to extreme measures to stop the pain being away from her is causing. But this girl, Freya, helps him get through it. What I didn’t like about this one was that I thought the relationship Freya and Oliver had was too quick and rushed. But, besides that detail (which is not-so-small), the story is overall good.<br />So basically, I enjoyed this book a lot. I didn’t love it, but I did like it a lot, and I recommend it to everyone who has read the books in the series. And to everyone who hasn’t read the series, I highly recommend them. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11079955091991401773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11740555978219864178">I decided to read Bloody Valentine by Melissa De La Cruze since it was right before Valentine’s Day. Immediately I was drawn to the story, which is divided into three mini stories. In the first story introduces Oliver, a young man who had just been dumped by his vampire girl-friend, Schuyler. He meets a beautiful angel in a bar and he is lead back to her apartment; where they sleep together and he forgets his feelings for the vampire. The second story goes back in time and is about Schuyler’s pa</span>
  <span id="freeText11740555978219864178" style="display:none">I decided to read Bloody Valentine by Melissa De La Cruze since it was right before Valentine’s Day. Immediately I was drawn to the story, which is divided into three mini stories. In the first story introduces Oliver, a young man who had just been dumped by his vampire girl-friend, Schuyler. He meets a beautiful angel in a bar and he is lead back to her apartment; where they sleep together and he forgets his feelings for the vampire. The second story goes back in time and is about Schuyler’s parents during their youth. Her mother was Queen of the Vampires; her father’s indent is not revealed but we see the two young men whom her mother loved. In the last and final story is back in the present and right before Schuyler’s wedding to the handsome vampire, Jack Force. But an evil force is out to try and kill Jack; they abduct Schuyler’s friends and make her promise to bring jack to them. But true love prevails and all the good live to see the wedding. This is a companion story but I didn’t feel like I missed anything by starting with this book.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676576829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11777263850494966838">I was pleasantly surprised with this novella! I really was not looking forward to it because the last novella in this serious Keys to the Repository was a bit of a let down and really just summed up the series at that point. But Bloody Valentine was really kind of an extension to Misguided Angel and followed its format of three parts.<br/><br/>Part one was Olivers story. He's having a difficult time getting over Schuyler because he is marked, and there was nothing he could do about it. The never ending fe</span>
  <span id="freeText11777263850494966838" style="display:none">I was pleasantly surprised with this novella! I really was not looking forward to it because the last novella in this serious Keys to the Repository was a bit of a let down and really just summed up the series at that point. But Bloody Valentine was really kind of an extension to Misguided Angel and followed its format of three parts.<br /><br />Part one was Olivers story. He's having a difficult time getting over Schuyler because he is marked, and there was nothing he could do about it. The never ending feeling of loss drive Oliver to some stupid and extreme limits.<br /><br />Part Two is about Allegra as a Teenager. This story was my favorite because I finally found out who her baby daddy was! Yup that's right...FINALLY we get to find out something about Schuyler's mysterious human father. We don't get the whole story but the little tidbits that I did get were enough to keep me interested. <br /><br />And the last story was about Schuyler and Jack and their adventures in Italy. I love that fact that Schuyler and Jack ended up together but their relationship is quickly turning nauseating. The I love you forever and calling each other my love and darling all the time is not romantic is having the opposite effect on me and it's grating my nerves. I'm hoping they will break up so I don't have to read about their "love" anymore. Ok maybe that was a little harsh..I don't really want them to break up but I do wish they would tone it down. <br /><br />Overall I really liked this novella, I just had to give it a 4 because of the cheesy romance between Jack and Schuyler. But I'm still rooting for them and looking forward to Lost in Time, the sixth book in the Blue Bloods Series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11777263850494966838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_713093035" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713093035" />
    <a title="Danylle DuPris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12735331-danylle-dupris"><img alt="Danylle DuPris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401371622p2/12735331.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713093035?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danylle DuPris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danylle DuPris" href="/user/show/12735331-danylle-dupris">Danylle DuPris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713093035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17809715097700950832">"Bloody Valentine" by Melissa de la Cruz was a fantastic book. Every event really came together. There are three different but intense parts in this book.<br/>Oliver has met a new girl, Freya. As they were talking in the pub, Oliver told her he had to go. He was going to go to the Blood house for forgotten familiars. As he soon realized, he changed his mind at the last second finding himself back at the pub to thank Freya. She took him back home and preformed a witches spell on Oliver to stop his lov</span>
  <span id="freeText17809715097700950832" style="display:none">"Bloody Valentine" by Melissa de la Cruz was a fantastic book. Every event really came together. There are three different but intense parts in this book.<br />Oliver has met a new girl, Freya. As they were talking in the pub, Oliver told her he had to go. He was going to go to the Blood house for forgotten familiars. As he soon realized, he changed his mind at the last second finding himself back at the pub to thank Freya. She took him back home and preformed a witches spell on Oliver to stop his love for Schuyler. It worked. He no longer feels the need to love her the way he never meant to.<br />In the second part of the book it takes place before the first book, "Blue Bloods". Allegra and Charles are in school at Endicott. Although they are twins, they don't look it. Allegra doesn't want her brother by her constantly. She wants to "blend" in with the Red Bloods. Bendix comes along and Allegra feels the need to be with him, to be his friend. The friendship only becomes more interesting as she starts to fall in love with him. Allegra sees the future of what her life will become.<br />Schuyler and Jack are to come together in the last part of the book. Will they be bonded together forever? Or will the Venators destroy their only chance?<br /><br />"Bloody Valentine" is told in first person by Schuyler, Oliver, and Allegra. Each character goes through a cycle of which they are to be bonded. Schuyler, as a half blood, is suppose to be abomination. She learns to love who she is and accept it, as does Jack. Oliver learned to accept who he is and that he shouldn't hold onto something that wasn't meant to be. Let it free, and if it comes back it's yours, if not, it was never meant to be. Allegra wasn't suppose to fall in love with a Red Blood, but taking the chance meant everything. The characters learn what is most important to them. They follow their hearts.<br /><br />"Bloody Valentine" takes place in Florence. Florence plays a big role in this book, because not only does it have a big part in history, all they events lead back to this place.<br /><br />There are a lot of themes in this book, but one to stand out the most is the will to follow what you love. Every character in this book realizes what they must do to follow their hearts.<br /><br />I definitely recommend this book to all the middle school and high school girls. They will fall in love with "Bloody Valentine" as well as the whole "Blue Bloods" series by Melissa de la Cruz.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13227057965469492416">Why oh why would I take this entire series on a holiday?!! I feel trapped with this series with no way it. When I got to the even of this "novella" (and I use that term VERY loosely Melissa de la Cruz-don't think I didn't notice the pages being 2/3 the size of every other book in the series and the "artwork" in the last chapter stretching this books page count!)I wanted to throw this book at someone (preferably its author). This book is really three short stories slapped together to explain a fe</span>
  <span id="freeText13227057965469492416" style="display:none">Why oh why would I take this entire series on a holiday?!! I feel trapped with this series with no way it. When I got to the even of this "novella" (and I use that term VERY loosely Melissa de la Cruz-don't think I didn't notice the pages being 2/3 the size of every other book in the series and the "artwork" in the last chapter stretching this books page count!)I wanted to throw this book at someone (preferably its author). This book is really three short stories slapped together to explain a few missing pieces of the story line (although it raises more questions than it answers for me). The title makes little sense to me? every one of these "stories" could have been easily worked into one of the Blue blood novels and certainly there was NO requirement to publish an entirely separate book, this could have been an epilogue or a prologue, or a footnote for that matter. This is clearly an author taking advantage of and insulting her readers intelligence, and she even shamelessly plugs her new spin off series in the middle of this tripe!!!! Tasteless to say the least and how embarrassing for her!! I got these books second hand or I would be demanding a refund, thankfully I am only out the garage sale price per book of 50 cents which still seems too much, I feel like the lady who sold them to me should have labelled them with some type of warning!! Personally, I will never seek out this authors material again, in fact I will avoid it at all costs! I have been reading each book praying for some sort of redeeming quality to this series which restore my faith in humanity (honestly with so many awesome indie authors not getting published how has she been allowed to keep turning out these affronts to modern literature relentlessly and without remorse) but sadly this is the sixth book and they have just progressively gotten worse. It is honestly and truly like this author doesn't even care!! She hasn't bothered to attempt to understand the mythology which exists in the fake world SHE created and cannot hold a consistent theme throughout and makes no attempt to cover up or explain away any of the gaping plot holes!! It is honestly like she has never sat down and read through her own work!!</span>

<div id="review_1219124868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219124868" />
    <a title="Liz Patino" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34636319-liz-patino"><img alt="Liz Patino" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495026273p2/34636319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219124868?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Patino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Patino" href="/user/show/34636319-liz-patino">Liz Patino</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219124868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14390879422896837674">Bloody Valentine was actually a pretty good book. This book was also written in three parts like the last book. The first part was about Oliver, the second was about when Allgera met Schuyler's father, and the last part was about Jack's and Schuyler's bonding. The first part was about Oliver, just like any other night in Suck City. Oliver was alone in New York trying to do something because of his loss of Schuyler from his life. He’s part of her and needs her to be around, but she’s now away in </span>
  <span id="freeText14390879422896837674" style="display:none">Bloody Valentine was actually a pretty good book. This book was also written in three parts like the last book. The first part was about Oliver, the second was about when Allgera met Schuyler's father, and the last part was about Jack's and Schuyler's bonding. The first part was about Oliver, just like any other night in Suck City. Oliver was alone in New York trying to do something because of his loss of Schuyler from his life. He’s part of her and needs her to be around, but she’s now away in Europe with Jack. Oliver finds a source of comfort in the most unlikely of places where random vampires come to drink his blood because he needed the pain. He was going crazy, but at that bar where he was, a witch was going to help him, but he did not know she was a witch. She gave him a potion in his food that made him not be in love with her anymore. The second part was in 1985 and tells how Schuyler’s mother (Allegra) first met her father. Allegra was young and a rebel. She met him at a hospital with a cast on his leg. He was a really cute guy and was going to leave the next day with her. After they left the hospital they started talking more. After the days passed they got together, and she got a sight that showed her future of her being in a coma and having a daughter. The third story, Ring of Fire, talks about Jack and Schuyler in current day Florence. The story is about Jack and Schuyler’s bonding ceremony. There’s a bit of action in the form of a Venator attack the day before the wedding, but no problems are encountered. They forced Schuyler to wear a necklace that would watch what she was doing. They also made her give Jack a ring that would shut down his powers, and only the ending of their love could break it. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone from ages 15-18, mostly girls because girls like romance books. I would highly recommend this book to people that like happy stories but at the same time sad stories.<br /><br />I gave this book a four star because it wasn't exactly what I was looking for, but it was a good book. Plus it finally told me what I always wanted to know, Oliver finally being free of Schuyler. Finally knew who Schuyler's father was. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14390879422896837674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_504777081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/504777081" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/504777081?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781423147299" href="/book/show/10087885-bloody-valentine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=angelology">angelology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer504777081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12130084265888338712"><b>”Bloody Valentine”</b> is a novella in the Blue Bloods series. It consists of three beautifully written short stories each with a focus on matters of the heart--hence the title. While it is not necessary to have read all the books in this series before reading this novella, it is recommended, as two of the three stories relate to events that take place in the previous two books. <br/><br/>The first story is about Schuyler Van Alen's friend and familiar Oliver Hazard-Perry and Freya, a character who will be th</span>
  <span id="freeText12130084265888338712" style="display:none"><b>”Bloody Valentine”</b> is a novella in the Blue Bloods series. It consists of three beautifully written short stories each with a focus on matters of the heart--hence the title. While it is not necessary to have read all the books in this series before reading this novella, it is recommended, as two of the three stories relate to events that take place in the previous two books. <br /><br />The first story is about Schuyler Van Alen's friend and familiar Oliver Hazard-Perry and Freya, a character who will be the focus of a new series by the author entitled <b>”Witches of East End”</b> (which I’ll probably check out to see it it’s worth reading). It is a wonderful story that fills in some of the missing pieces on what's going on with Oliver at the same time as other things are occurring in <b>”Misguided Angel”</b>. <br /><br />The second story brings us back to 1985 where we get to meet a young Allegra Van Alen and the human familiar she falls in love with, Bendix Chase. This is a great addition as it gives further insight into Schuyler's parents and just how she came to be. I really enjoyed this story since thus far in the series we haven’t been given much info about Allegra’s life before being in the hospital. <br /><br />The final story, and the longest, is about Schuyler Van Alen and Jack Force and their bonding ceremony which occurs after the events in <b>”Misguided Angel”</b>. This is a great way to close this book as it gives readers another opportunity to see Jack and Schuyler and witness their love for one another. It bridges the long gap between the previous book and the next book in the series, <b>”Lost in Time”</b>, which won't be out until October.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong the content was as great as always, but the style of the books has changed a lot and they seem to be getting shorter and shorter.<br /><br /><br />More of Purplycookie’s Reviews @: <b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/purplycookie">http://www.goodreads.com/purplycookie</a> </b><br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> Bloody Valentine (A Blue Bloods Book)<br /><u>Author</u> Melissa De La Cruz<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="12130084265888338712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144051652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144051652" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1945325-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301006382p2/1945325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144051652?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/1945325-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1945325-debbie?shelf=flowers">flowers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144051652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3305143168597789041">If you are a fan of the Blue Bloods series then you will definitely enjoy this one. It's a short and quick read and is made up of three short stories. It was somewhat of a surprise to me that I enjoyed all three as I'm usually not a short story fan and in a book like I rarely find myself liking all the stories. I suppose I shouldn't have been too surprised since I am a huge fan of Melissa de la Cruz's writing. <br/><br/>One story follows Oliver as he struggles to deal with his love for Schuyler and the co</span>
  <span id="freeText3305143168597789041" style="display:none">If you are a fan of the Blue Bloods series then you will definitely enjoy this one. It's a short and quick read and is made up of three short stories. It was somewhat of a surprise to me that I enjoyed all three as I'm usually not a short story fan and in a book like I rarely find myself liking all the stories. I suppose I shouldn't have been too surprised since I am a huge fan of Melissa de la Cruz's writing. <br /><br />One story follows Oliver as he struggles to deal with his love for Schuyler and the consequences of letting her go. We also see the introduction of one of the characters, Freya, in Melissa's new series the Witches of East End. My heart ached for Oliver and I was glad when it ended the way it did. Freya looks like she is going to be an interesting character in this new series and I can't wait to read more about her and her sisters.<br /><br />Another story follows Schuyler's mother when she was a "teenager" and meets Schuyler's father. I enjoyed this one but it definitely left you wanting more and I couldn't believe it ended where it did. I really wanted to see more of Schuyler's father and what happens between him and Allegra.<br /><br />The third story follows Jack and Schuyler as they are on the run and we actually get to see their joining. Schuyler showed some kick ass skills and the ending definitely leaves you hungering to find out what is going to happen with Jack when he confronts Mimi.<br /><br />All three stories were phenomenal and will leave you anxiously waiting for the sixth Blue Bloods book, Lost in Time, due out in October and her new series The Witches of East End which has it's first book due out June 2011. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3305143168597789041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119429375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119429375" />
    <a title="Grace Mycek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3971859-grace-mycek"><img alt="Grace Mycek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455110278p2/3971859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119429375?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace Mycek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace Mycek" href="/user/show/3971859-grace-mycek">Grace Mycek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3971859-grace-mycek?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3971859-grace-mycek?shelf=disliked">disliked</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119429375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3780824877914030838">Ok, well that took about an hour to read, if that. I don't know about this series. As it goes on, I'm getting increasingly disinterested in it. The character development was very nicely done in the first few books...but now the characters fall flat on the pages. I use to really like Schuyler's character because she was independent and did her own thing. Now she's so dependent on Jack it's nauseating. <br/><br/>I also don't understand this whole half book between the actual book thing (the keys to the repo</span>
  <span id="freeText3780824877914030838" style="display:none">Ok, well that took about an hour to read, if that. I don't know about this series. As it goes on, I'm getting increasingly disinterested in it. The character development was very nicely done in the first few books...but now the characters fall flat on the pages. I use to really like Schuyler's character because she was independent and did her own thing. Now she's so dependent on Jack it's nauseating. <br /><br />I also don't understand this whole half book between the actual book thing (the keys to the repository, bloody valentine). If Cruz just added some more details they could basically be their own books in the series. Maybe it's just me but these books feel so rushed with all the information she tries to cram into it. I would have liked to see the fight scene between Jack and the venators in more detail, but it just happens and bam it's done. <br /><br /><br />I also didn't like how Allegra was portrayed in this book. We don't really know much about Allegra because for almost the whole series she has been in a coma, but as Cruz writes of Allegra before the coma happened, she just seemed annoying and selfish. She treated Charles like crap when all he did was love her as was supposed to happen in their subsequent lifetimes which made me really start to dislike Allegra's character.<br /><br /><br />I feel like Cruz would be better off in making these full books instead of in-between books. This one was interesting but I had those issues with it. I guess we'll just have to see where the next blue bloods book takes me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3780824877914030838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9IrlHSNSUk7kFGaAvseC4zd0wLgnYFyVerXY4Ra3JhB1q7wn8m64Xk0uPGCrkVs8uJXn4DDlpUPYy1fEQ/LvzA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4Pa0vQthg71ww8H9GfskPDDo4Ua/edBDR4Wco+9PbMhh1+2H2l1prdn5mx0Mrf3jvwnGHqj8KZXl+xOGugqlFA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18054592609899083230">Melissa de la Cruz is the New York Times and USA Today best-selling author of many critically acclaimed and award-winning novels for teens including The Au Pairs series, the Blue Bloods series, the Ashleys series, the Angels on Sunset Boulevard series and the semi-autobiographical novel Fresh off the Boat.<br/><br/>Her books for adults include the novel Cat’s Meow, the anthology Girls Who Like Boys Who Like</span>
  <span id="freeText18054592609899083230" style="display:none">Melissa de la Cruz is the New York Times and USA Today best-selling author of many critically acclaimed and award-winning novels for teens including The Au Pairs series, the Blue Bloods series, the Ashleys series, the Angels on Sunset Boulevard series and the semi-autobiographical novel Fresh off the Boat.<br /><br />Her books for adults include the novel Cat’s Meow, the anthology Girls Who Like Boys Who Like Boys and the tongue-in-chic handbooks How to Become Famous in Two Weeks or Less and The Fashionista Files: Adventures in Four-inch heels and Faux-Pas.<br /><br />She has worked as a fashion and beauty editor and has written for many publications including The New York Times, Marie Claire, Harper’s Bazaar, Glamour, Cosmopolitan, Allure, The San Francisco Chronicle, McSweeney’s, Teen Vogue, CosmoGirl! and Seventeen. She has also appeared as an expert on fashion, trends and fame for CNN, E! and FoxNews.<br /><br />Melissa grew up in Manila and moved to San Francisco with her family, where she graduated high school salutatorian from The Convent of the Sacred Heart. She majored in art history and English at Columbia University (and minored in nightclubs and shopping!).<br /><br />She now divides her time between New York and Los Angeles, where she lives in the Hollywood Hills with her husband and daughter. </span>
